Jiaotong University Volleyball Season Opens; Fudan and Jinan Triumph; Fudan Crushes Chizhi in Straight Sets; Jinan Overcomes Guanghua Three Sets to Two 127

The 9th Jiaotong University Men's Volleyball Championship opened yesterday at 3:00 PM at Guanghua and Chizhi Schools, respectively. (The women's division was cancelled this year.) Participating schools include Fudan, Jinan, Chizhi, and Guanghua. Compared to the era of the eight major universities in the Jiangnan region in previous years, the feeling is quite different. The results of yesterday's two matches are as follows:

Fudan Defeats Chizhi 128

The first set of the match between Fudan and Chizhi was held at the Guangdong East Middle School Gymnasium yesterday at 3:00 PM. After the start of the match, Fudan took the lead, with Zhou Dayun soaring high and scoring five points in a row. Chizhi was unwilling to fall behind, and Zhang Jiayi scored a point. However, Fudan's momentum remained strong, with Qiu Guangxie and Zhou Jiemin scoring repeatedly, one smashing and one spiking. At this point, Chizhi suffered a setback. Fudan won the first set 21-3.

Second set: Chizhi's Yu Wenquan served, immediately scoring a point. Wang Chen added icing on the cake, also achieving remarkable feats. Fudan quickly took an 8-4 lead. Seeing that the situation was unfavorable, all of Chizhi's players calmly responded to the challenge. Mai Zhihong and Wang Yufu rose together, their momentum flourishing, and they tied the score at 8-8. Afterwards, the game tied again several times. When Fudan took the lead at 20-19, Chen Zongqi added another point, winning the set 21-19.

Third set: Fudan won two consecutive sets, their morale soaring. When the front line seized Chizhi's incoming ball, Zhou Dayun immediately seized the opportunity to score a point. Chizhi's Zhang Jiayi was unwilling to show weakness, leaping forward on the front line and striking a blow, immediately retaliating. However, Fudan did not diminish its courage and remained aggressive. The score soared like a blue cloud, and after three rounds, they were already leading by 18-13. Zhou Dayun added three points, winning again with a score of 21-13. In total, Chizhi suffered a disastrous defeat with a score of 3-0.

Jinan Defeats Guanghua 129

Guanghua Dominates: The match between Jinan and Guanghua was held at Guanghua yesterday, starting at 3:30 PM. The strength of the two teams was evenly matched. Guanghua's front and middle rows were extremely sharp in smashing, but the back row was weaker. Jinan's ability to save dangerous balls in the back row was truly miraculous. After the start of the match, Jinan scored two points first with a serve, then advanced to 4-1. Guanghua caught up step by step and tied the score. Afterwards, each side made progress, but only by one or two points. Soon, Guanghua took the lead with 11-9 and gained the right to switch sides first. At 12-10, Jinan surpassed them with 15-12. Guanghua then fought calmly, from 17-17 to 20-20. Finally, Guanghua scored two points in a row and won the first set 22-20. In the second set, Guanghua again led with 5-1, giving Jinan a huge blow. Xuan Yaoji's serve turned the tide, and Jinan surpassed them with 6-5, and took the right to switch sides first with 11-10. Jinan's host saw that Guanghua's momentum was strong and urgently called in captain Yuan Zejian to replace Rong Yaoji. Unexpectedly, this change was met with oppression from Guanghua, until 18-18, Guanghua won the second set with 21-18.

Jinan Triumphs: Jinan lost two consecutive sets. The third set was a critical juncture. Li Yaoji was again called up to replace Liu Boxi, and the morale soared, leading with 6-1. However, Guanghua was not weak either, approaching step by step. The two sides rescued dangerous balls with great brilliance. Jinan used all their might and finally won a set with 21-11. In the fourth set, Guanghua took the lead with 7-2. Fortunately, Jinan's back row provided strong support, scoring eight points in a row, surpassing them with 10-7. Guanghua saw that the situation was not good and urgently called up new forces to enter the game. At this time, the situation was in a storm. When Guanghua took the lead with 17-15, the situation changed again. However, Jinan's ball delivery was fast and powerful, and they quickly won a set with 21-17. At this time, a 2-2 situation was formed. In the fifth set, Guanghua worked hard to capture it. Tang Zhiwei scored five points in a row with a serve, causing Jinan to lose their color. Yuan Zejian had superb skills and fought hard, one point after another, catching up to 4-4 and then 6-6. Then, they reached 10-10. After the side exchange, Jinan Father Ti Zeng added 14 points, and Guanghua began to panic. After that, Jinan became smoother, ending the set with 21-14 in an instant. Jinan won three sets in a row, turning defeat into victory with 3-2. The lineup and results are recorded below.

National Children's Painting Exhibition Regulations; Methods for Exhibit Display and Review; Joint Meeting of Review and Display Groups Held Yesterday; Exhibition Hall Divided into Zones with Each Province and City as a Zone 140

The Preparatory Committee of the National Children's Painting Exhibition held a joint meeting of the Review and Display Groups at Shangwen Primary School at 3:00 PM yesterday. The attendees included Yan Kechang, Sun Yongyi, Chuan Boliang, Xie Haiyan, Tan Chuanwei, Shi Wenbin, Cheng Jiahe, Shi Chongpeng, Huang Ruozhou, Pan Shouheng, Yan Keding, Lin Guifu, Pan Yuzhong, Zhang Meisun, Guan Kun and Qian Honglie, and Qian Fugong, the representative of the Preparatory Committee. Resolutions of the Joint Meeting: The "Exhibit Display Method" was passed; resolved to amend and pass it. The "Exhibit Review Method" was passed; resolved to amend and pass it. Resolved that the Review Group Director would allocate responsibilities for the review of exhibits by each group. Resolved that the Review Group would formulate separate methods for evaluating and awarding prizes for children's painting performances. Resolved that the Preparatory Committee should determine the transportation expenses for Review and Display Group staff to attend meetings; resolved to pass it. Resolved to set the office hours for Display Group staff to attend meetings; resolved that staff should be assigned to attend meetings daily from May 15th. Resolved that the Display Group would be responsible for the design and management of the painting mounting process.

Exhibit Display Method: The exhibits on display are limited to those that have been reviewed and selected. The venue will be divided into several zones, with each province and city as a display unit. The works displayed in each zone will be further divided according to the classification of exhibits. Within each group of exhibits, the order of display will be determined by the age level of the children. A separate exhibition room will be opened for the display of works by painters for children to appreciate. Each exhibition room should be numbered and a description posted at the entrance. Plan the route and signs of the venue. Manage the layout of the children's painting performance venue.

Exhibit Review Method: The exhibits of this exhibition will be reviewed according to the exhibit review standards. All exhibits will first be compiled by the Compilation Group according to the following allocation methods: (A) Each province and city will be a unit; (B) The exhibits of each unit will be further divided according to the classification of exhibits. The exhibits of each group will be further divided according to the age level of the children. According to the exhibit list, the preliminary selection will be held in groups by all the review personnel. After the preliminary selection, a final selection will be held jointly by all the review personnel. The selected works of the final selection will still be listed in the exhibit catalogue according to the above-mentioned group classification and level division. Review will begin on May 15th and will be convened by the Director of the Review Group. In addition to the full-time staff of the Review Group, the Review Committee members in Shanghai will also be invited to participate. Every review should be recorded.

Details of public education facilities in middle schools in this city have been investigated by personnel dispatched by the City Party Department. The current directors of moral education and civic teachers have also been investigated and listed by the Qualification Examination Committee for Directors of Moral Education and Civic Teachers in this city, and submitted to the educational administration agencies for reference. The Shanghai News Agency interviewed Committee Member Yu Zhongbiao of the committee yesterday, and learned that the majority of the public education personnel currently employed in middle schools are registered and qualified. The committee, in accordance with the provisions of Article 3 of the examination regulations promulgated by the Central Government, will issue a notice to all schools that unregistered civic teachers and moral education directors are not allowed to be employed, in order to maintain laws and regulations.

Lei Zhen Speaks on "Nation and Culture" 148

(I)

At 5:30 PM on the 24th, the Nanjing branch of the China Cultural Construction Association invited Central Committee member Lei Zhen to deliver a speech titled "Nation and Culture" at the Central Broadcasting Station. The following is a transcript of his original words: "For a group to become a nation, it must possess unique natural attributes and culture. This is an undeniable conclusion. Today, when one speaks of a nation, it seems like a self-evident concept, but if one were to ask what exactly a nation is, diverse opinions abound and are difficult to reconcile.

From a natural perspective, blood lineage and territory are important factors in the formation of a nation. However, the so-called nation today, no matter how much heterogeneity is mixed and unified within it, a nation of pure blood is practically nonexistent today. The same goes for territory. The people of China and England are scattered all over the world, yet their national character has not disappeared. A nation that resides in only one place is now an exception. Due to the limitations of the topic, the factors of race and territory cannot be discussed in detail; only the relationship between nation and culture will be addressed. Moreover, with the progress of modern transportation and frequent human interaction, blood lineage and territory are no longer crucial conditions for studying national characteristics. Culture is the key factor that represents the characteristics of a nation. The definition of a nation given by Bluntschli is: 'A nation is a union of a multitude of people belonging to a particular race who are bound together by a community of spirit and feeling evoked by language and customs, social systems with various professions and social classes, and who have a shared civilization. This civilization sets aside the ties of the state and gives them a unified concept, making them feel distinct from people of other countries.'

Among the elements of culture, sciences, technology, economics, and other aspects related to reason have universal qualities and a weaker connection to the nation. A nation can certainly be proud of its intellectual superiority over other nations, but this does not necessarily increase love for one's own nation. A nation with lower knowledge not only does not despise itself because of this but also often has a stronger solidarity than a nation with higher knowledge. The reason for this is quite evident.

In primitive times, religion held enormous power. Therefore, religious rituals and creeds often determined the factors of a nation. Totemic societies invariably revolved around religion, and it can be said that the nation was united only by religion. However, since the advent of civilization, with the expansion of politics, economics, and other forces, the power of religion has gradually diminished. Various European nations, all adherents of Christianity, have not been able to merge into one large nation because of this. Instead, due to the division of each nation, rifts have arisen within Christianity (initially dividing into Greek Orthodox and Roman Orthodox, and later into Protestant and Catholic). Since the Wei and Jin dynasties, the Chinese nation has not only juxtaposed Confucianism, Buddhism, and Taoism, with emperors assigning them each a designation, allowing the people to freely practice their beliefs, but even bizarre and outlandish religions could coexist without conflict. The nation not only did not separate because of this but also expanded further and became more unified. Coming to the present day, the separation of nations based on differences in religious beliefs is limited to a few uncivilized nations.

Then, what is the most important factor determining a nation? A shared way of life in historical destiny, and the unity of language and script are the most important of these three. Now, without discussing their interplay, let's separate them into three aspects and examine them individually.

First, a shared historical destiny is the foundation for the formation of a nation. Because sharing weal and woe in history causes people belonging to this group to develop a consciousness of a common life. Thus, internally, it consolidates their unity, becoming a single unit, and externally, it uses its entire strength to contend with other nations. Bluntschli said, 'In our view, a nation is a soul, a spirit, that comes from remembering past sacrifices, glory, repeated prosperity, and shared sorrow. A spiritual family, in the present, comes from the desire to continue maintaining a shared life. The things that constitute a nation are neither because of speaking the same language nor because of belonging to the same racial group. It is due to having jointly accomplished great undertakings in the past and still desiring to accomplish great undertakings in the future. A nation is a spiritual principle that is the result of deep and complex historical circumstances.' Our ancestors, whether in culture or politics, built great achievements as a common bond for our nation. At the same time, since the beginning of history, we have also suffered many sorrows. In the same period, we were invaded by the Xiongnu and Quanrong. Since the Qin and Han dynasties, foreign interactions have become increasingly frequent. The greatest defeats were the Three Catastrophes: the Five Barbarians invasion of China and the rule of the Yuan and Qing dynasties. The first catastrophe caused China to split into North and South for nearly three hundred years. The second catastrophe led to national subjugation for over eighty years. The third catastrophe lasted for as long as two hundred and sixty years. However, although the duration differed, sharing weal and woe was undeniable.

School Survey

An Overview of the Shanghai German School (I) 149

— Hu Zuyin

The German community in Shanghai has established a German school. The school is located at No. 1 Da Xi Road in the western district of the International Settlement; it is large-scale and perfectly equipped. The author is grateful to Dr. Weber, the principal of the school, for providing various materials and for the gift of a commemorative publication and school overview.

1. The Oldest German School in the Far East

The Shanghai German School has been in operation for forty-one years. In the summer of 1894, a German missionary recruited about a dozen German children to teach in his home. Soon the number of students increased to about twenty; thus, preparations were made to open a school. After active progress, the oldest German school in the Far East was officially established on April 1, 1895. Initially, the school had only three teachers and twenty-three students; later, it gradually developed, and by 1900, the number of students had increased to more than forty. Soon, the German church began construction, and it was decided to build a school building behind the church; in the autumn of 1901, the school moved into its self-built school building and started classes.

A few years later, the school continued to develop, and the original school building was no longer sufficient. The old school's various facilities were not hygienic, there was no sports field, and students often played on the streets after class, which was inappropriate. In 1905, Emperor Wilhelm II of Germany celebrated his silver jubilee, and the German community in Shanghai donated funds to celebrate. Considering the large number of German children in Shanghai who needed schooling but lacked modern school buildings, the Emperor decided to return the celebratory gifts donated by the German community to be used to purchase land in Shanghai for the purpose of building a new school building. Thus, in 1906, the German community in Shanghai purchased more than ten acres of land on Da Xi Road (the current school site) and decided to name the future new German school the Kaiser-Wilhelm School to commemorate the Emperor's kindness in donating the land.

Since then, the school has undergone various changes and developments; now, a few important facts are presented for narration. Previously, the school affairs were handled jointly with the church affairs, which both parties felt was inappropriate; in 1908, the school separated from the church, and the administration became completely independent. Later, after various difficulties and efforts, the new school building was officially completed on Da Xi Road on April 23, 1911. On that day, the entire German community in Shanghai came to the new school building to hold a celebration. In the same year, it was decided to add a kindergarten. At this time, the total number of students in the school had increased to more than one hundred. The European War broke out in 1914. In February 1922, the school began to return to normal.

In 1928, the German community believed that the original school building was no longer sufficient for the school's development, so it was decided to demolish the old school building and rebuild a large-scale new school building. In May 1929, the large-scale new school building was completed, and the foundation of the school could be considered solidified at that time. The school currently has one year of kindergarten, four years of elementary school, and nine years of secondary school. The school is currently recognized by the German government, and students can participate in the German national examination after graduating from secondary school. The school currently has 260 students, 140 boys and 120 girls; among them, 90 are non-German students who wish to study at the school. There are a total of 18 teachers in the school, including 14 full-time teachers and 4 part-time teachers. The purpose of the school is to enable the children of the German community in Shanghai to avoid the influence of foreign education and to provide them with an opportunity to absorb German science and knowledge so that they can become useful German citizens. The success of the school today demonstrates the strong will and continuous efforts of the German expatriate community; at the same time, in the international environment of Shanghai, the establishment of the school can also enhance Germany's international equality.

Commercial News

Gold Loan Interest at 4% 150

Since our country implemented the legal tender policy, various interest rates have naturally followed suit and fallen. Currently, the foreign exchange swap difference is extremely small, but the gold loan swap still requires the sellers to post 4 to 5 yuan monthly. In the current period, some sellers have even posted 5.5 yuan, which amounts to a monthly interest rate of over 0.5%. Later, with the repeated efforts of the financial community to maintain stability, it began to stabilize. This was due to fourth quarter relationships (which caused a brief surge in seller activity). Recently, because the four major banks, including a certain bank, jointly posted spot and swaps in large quantities, the posted price has now dropped to around 4 yuan, with a monthly interest rate of less than 4% (gold loan price over 1100 yuan, swap at 4 yuan and 5 cents). However, sellers are still crowded, taking advantage of the low price to post, and the overall trend seems to be stabilizing. Tracing back to the original reasons, there are approximately four: 1. Abundant spot reserves, making it impossible for sellers to collect goods (which can be inferred from the chips in the gold exchange); 2. After the legal tender policy, there are more people in the industry with an upward mindset, leading to crowded long positions; 3. Spot goods frequently arrive in Shanghai to seek resale (most of the sellers recently posting are spot houses, and not general surplus long positions); 4. Among the Tianjin gangs, there are even many who swap spot gold for cash due to headquarter transfers; 5. Gold loan mortgages require 4.5% interest from foreign banks (still with discounts), and they also require an appropriate discount on the gold price. Generally, buyers must advance a portion of the cash. Because of this, although gold loan swaps exist, the financial community is rushing to arbitrage, and the posted price ultimately requires a monthly interest rate of around 4%.

If the Fourth Quarter is Prolonged, the Deposit Interest Rate is 5.5 Yuan, and the Lowest Overdue Interest Rate is 8 Yuan 154

Every year in April and October, the financial community is busy with the settlement of long-term transactions as usual. This year, due to the continued sluggish market, lending is restricted and borrowing is hopeless. Although efforts are made on the surface to maintain stability and turn danger into safety, the actual hidden tightness is much greater than before. It is found that the total amount of the fourth quarter initial period (excluding those that have been settled) and the amount of deposits transferred by various depositors reached more than 23 million. The total amount of long-term overdue loans is more than 50 million, plus 13 to 14 million long-term Yongzhuang loans and more than 25 million long-term mortgages. The total settlement difference is more than 10 million. Currently, with the authorities' accommodation to transfer and settle interest without repaying the principal, they account for more than 80% to 90% of the total, and those who pay are actually less than 5 million. From this, one can see the dryness of the market. In addition, new long-term loans are very rare. Except for banks such as Zizhong, Guanghua, Daya, Huizhong, Zhonghe, Zhengming, Jiangzhe, and other banks that are members of the Bankers' Association, and qianzhuang such as Chengyu, Gengyu, Fuyuan, Fukang, Anyu, Ankang, Cunde, Duyu, Jintai, Tongyu, Shunkang, Wufeng, and Zifeng, who still release huge long-term loans, amounting to more than 10 million, other types only accept and do not release. Therefore, apart from the more troublesome transfer procedures for old accounts, there is really nothing to do, and there is not much difference from the usual busyness and leisure. Therefore, this year's fourth-quarter situation is far less busy than last year, but the procedures for settlement are indeed more difficult than last year. Often, the amount owed by one account involves more than a dozen trips back and forth, and it is impossible to recover it as desired in one stroke. In terms of the recovery of long-term loans from Yongzhuang, only a few percent of the overdue loans are recovered from the huge amount of thousands of millions. If the market is relaxed, with such tight conditions in Yong City, why would one not want to recover the loans? The long-term overdue loans that cannot be largely recovered and the total cost of interest are examined. The highest amount of the Hankou Gang is 12.5 yuan, which cannot be used as an exception. The highest amount of the loan interest rate for other gangs is no more than 10.05 yuan, and the lowest interest rate is still 8 yuan, which seems to be slightly higher than the previous price of 7.5 yuan.

Overview of Cotton Yarn Delivery in April 157

Yarn: 2,500 bales...Yarn merchants deliver goods; Cotton: Over 90,000 piculs...Tong Kee receives.

The April contract for Golden Rooster brand yarn was priced at 193.9 yuan on November 1st of last year. At that time, the market trend was steadily improving, and the overall outlook was good. The speculative fervor over gold prices was intense, leading to a surge of positive news. Coupled with a reduction in yarn inventory in this city, market prices steadily climbed to a peak. After the implementation of the new currency policy on November 4th, prices jumped by ten yuan in a single session, exceeding 200 yuan. Subsequently, fierce competition between bullish and bearish factions resulted in significant fluctuations. The situation then shifted due to changes in the European political landscape, with escalating tensions between Italy and Abyssinia causing overseas yarn and cotton prices to soar. Speculative yarn prices rose sharply, reaching a peak of 212 yuan on December 4th. However, as the year-end approached, parties began to close positions, and warehouse yarn inventory exceeded 280,000 bales, causing the market price to fall back to the 200 yuan level. By mid-March, due to the development of spring sales and a surge in Japanese yarn prices, gold traders and securities brokers, seeing stagnation in their own businesses, flocked to the yarn and cotton market, driving up demand and prices. High prices reached 209.3 yuan. Unexpectedly, yarn sales slowed down, and the bearish side took advantage of ample supply, with warehouse yarn inventory reaching 31,800 bales. This threatened the market, causing it to decline to 201.6 yuan. However, Mr. Sheng's intention to take delivery remained firm. The final session price was 204.1 yuan, still up 10.02 yuan from the initial price. As a result, the remaining amount to be delivered was 10,005 bales, an increase of 1,300 bales compared to the previous month. The delivery price, calculated based on the final three days, was 203 yuan, one yuan lower than the previous month. Delivered goods included 1,000 bales of 20-count Golden Rooster new yarn, 700 bales of Great Flying艇, and 600 bales of Red Kui Xing, totaling 2,300 bales. The rest were self-delivered. It is said that Mr. Sheng and gold arbitrageurs were the majority of the receivers, while yarn merchants were the majority of the deliverers. The situation then shifted due to the European situation, and the formal announcement of the new currency on October 4th ignited a frenzy in the market, with prices soaring by three yuan in a single session to 43 yuan. Prices then hovered at a high level, reaching a peak of 45.95 yuan on December 4th. Seafood: Straw Mushrooms and Agar-Agar in Season to Prevent Mold 164

Straw mushrooms, also known as 自生, are also called 北口. They are divided into two types: large and small. In the north, they are called 大自生 and 中自生, while in the south they are called 大口蔴 and 小口丁. They are produced in northern China and Mongolia, with those from 裏八旗 considered the best. The annual production volume is around 1,000 piculs, but in years of poor harvest, it is only 500 to 600 piculs. As things are valued when scarce, the value is high, and only those with means can afford them. The most prosperous sales locations are Tianjin, Hankou, Sichuan, Fujian, and Guangdong, followed by this city and Hangzhou, Suzhou, Ningbo, and other places, where sales are also quite significant. Currently, high-quality 大口蔴 sells for 950 to 920 yuan, ordinary goods for 800 to 760 to 70 yuan, 裏八旗 small 口丁 for 820 yuan, and high-quality goods from other regions for 650 to 660 yuan, with the lowest only 470 to 80 yuan. Currently, there is not much inventory in the entire street, and the market situation is quite stable. However, the rainy season is approaching, and the goods must be protected from moisture. If they are not stored properly, they can easily change color, and once reworked, there is no good solution. Fortunately, with the development of science, there are cold storage facilities, so those who store more have already stored them in cold storage, preparing for sales in autumn and winter.

Agar-agar arrivals are gradually increasing, but as the weather is gradually getting warmer, business from客帮 is also showing signs of life. Markets such as Hunan, Hubei, Sichuan, Henan, and this street are more lively than before, and the market atmosphere is thus colored. Yesterday's prices from industry insiders (天雪) 300 yuan, (單雪) (氷淸) (金鶴) 295 yuan, (銀雪) (白燕) 292 yuan, (光雪) (白天) 288 yuan, (白玉) (玉潔) 280 yuan, (白龍) (玉池) 265 yuan.

Popular Lecture

Su Zhou, the Beard 174

— Su Zihan

Near the end of the Ming Dynasty, a very righteous woodcutter appeared in Dongting Mountain, Suzhou. No one knew his surname or given name, but because he was tall and had a full beard, everyone called him Beard Woodcutter. Beard Woodcutter was very strong. Others could only carry 100 catties, but he could carry 240 catties, but he still sold it at the price of 100 catties. Someone asked him why he did that, and he said, "Anyway, the firewood comes from the mountains, and it only depends on strength, without any capital. Although I am strong, my appetite is no bigger than others, so why sell it for more money?"

Beard Woodcutter was illiterate, but he liked to listen to others talk about past events. Because he was straightforward, he liked loyal ministers and righteous people, and hated treacherous ministers and villains. Sometimes his criticism of the rights and wrongs of people in the past was very accurate, and those who studied medicine and understood etiquette were no better than that.

Once, there was a theatrical performance in the village. Beard Woodcutter was returning from the mountains with firewood and passed under the stage. The stage was performing The Story of Yue Fei, and Qin Hui had just come out. The actor playing Qin Hui played it perfectly, like a living traitor. Beard Woodcutter watched and couldn't restrain his anger. He jumped onto the stage with a flying leap, knocked down the actor playing Qin Hui with a palm, held him down, and rained blows on him with his fists and feet, hitting him until his head was broken and bleeding. People nearby managed to persuade him to stop. Beard Woodcutter still shouted, "He became a prime minister, but he framed loyal people and ruined the country. It's too good for him that he isn't beaten to death!"

Someone nearby said, "This is just a play, it's fake."

Beard Woodcutter said, "I know it's fake, that's why I'm beating him. If it were real, I would have chopped him up long ago!"

Beard Woodcutter was also not superstitious. One of his older brothers went to Maoshan to worship, fell off a cliff, and died. Some superstitious people said that because his brother drank wine and was not sincere, he was beaten to death by Wang Lingguan with a golden whip. When Beard Woodcutter heard this, he rushed to Maoshan day and night. He deliberately got very drunk, ran to the hall, pointed at the statue of Wang Lingguan, and cursed, "You are a real piece of trash, using the guise of the patriarch to act like a tyrant here! My brother came to offer incense, which was a good intention, and drinking wine is not a capital crime. Why did you kill him? Today, I'm not only not offering incense, but I'm also here drunk, see if you dare to do anything to me! Dare to kill me? Hmph, I guess you wouldn't dare. Why are you staring at me and waving your whip? Fine, I'll just smash your damn whip and smash your mother-loving face!"

As soon as Beard Woodcutter finished speaking, he was about to jump up and snatch the whip from Wang Lingguan's hand. The incense-worshippers around him desperately stopped him. Afterward, Beard Woodcutter moved his brother's body back home.

At that time, there was a man named Chen Xueqi living in Dongting Mountain. His parents had both passed away, and he had been betrothed to a girl surnamed Zou since he was a child. The date had already been set, and they were about to get married when Zou girl's older brother suddenly changed his mind. He was a snob and did not allow Zou girl to marry into the Chen family, but instead offered her to a wealthy local gentleman in Suzhou as a concubine. When Chen Xueqi heard about this, he was frantic and rushed to the city to file a lawsuit. But officials protect each other, and the official was also afraid of the wealthy gentleman's influence and dared not do anything. Chen Xueqi also sued Zou girl's older brother, but the official refused and instead kicked him out. The officials don't care about this kind of thing, so who would dare to stand up? Chen Xueqi was so anxious that he had nowhere to turn.

One day, Chen Xueqi met Beard Woodcutter on the road and told him about the whole thing, and said, "I have long heard that you are very righteous and willing to help people. Now that I have encountered such a heartbreaking thing, can you help me think of a way?"

Beard Woodcutter thought for a moment and said, "Alright. But this matter cannot be done in three or two days, you must wait."

When Chen Xueqi heard Beard Woodcutter's promise, he quickly knelt down and kowtowed, saying, "You are a really good person! If I can meet my wife, then you will be my reborn parents."

Beard Woodcutter said, "You are too kind! It is nothing," as he helped Chen Xueqi up.

Although Beard Woodcutter was illiterate, he was also a meticulous man. He knew that if he wanted to rescue Zou girl, he had to go to the wealthy gentleman's house. A household like the wealthy gentleman's was not easy to enter, but Beard Woodcutter had a plan.

Beard Woodcutter ran to the city and found a human trafficker's house. He pretended to say that he had come to find someone to help him find work, that he had a lot of strength, and that he would be best as a sedan chair carrier. Soon after, Beard Woodcutter actually went to work as a sedan chair carrier at the wealthy gentleman's house. Because he was strong and worked diligently, the wealthy gentleman liked him very much and even allowed him to enter and exit the inner courtyard at will.

After some time, Beard Woodcutter already knew that the third concubine was Zou girl. As soon as he had the opportunity, he would discuss it with her.

One day, Beard Woodcutter ran into Zou girl in the back courtyard. There was no one around, which was a good opportunity to talk. Beard Woodcutter quickly walked up to her and said in a low voice, "Zou girl, you are living a very comfortable life now, but do you still remember Chen Lang?"

Zou girl was suddenly shocked to see an unfamiliar old man saying this to her. "Who are you?" she asked.

Beard Woodcutter said, "Girl, don't you recognize me? I am Beard Woodcutter, and Chen Lang asked me to inquire about your news. Chen Lang misses you very much!"

Zou girl calmed herself and said, "Sir, how can I leave Chen Lang behind! I originally wanted to find a way to die, but I couldn't escape from that murderer. He had many people, and he had them tie up my hands and feet and strip off my clothes. He defiled me that very night. I am truly sorry for Chen Lang! It's good that you came, sir. I beg you to rescue me and let me meet Chen Lang. I would be willing to die!" As she spoke, she burst into tears.

Beard Woodcutter quickly said, "Girl, there is no need to be like this. There are many eyes and ears here. Anyway, I will do my best."

A long time passed. One day, the wealthy gentleman's wife wanted to take the concubines to tour Tianping Mountain. When Beard Woodcutter heard about it, he thought to himself, "The opportunity has come!" So he first went to the riverside to hire a boat before going back to carry the sedan chair. He intentionally carried the third sedan chair, in which Zou girl was sitting. That sedan chair carrier had also been bribed by Beard Woodcutter.

As soon as they left the city, Beard Woodcutter took another fork in the road and rushed towards the river like the wind. The servants who were following saw that something was wrong and also shouted and rushed after them. Beard Woodcutter arrived at the river, put down the sedan chair, helped Zou girl out, and helped her onto the boat. The pursuers also arrived. The sedan chair carrier had already left. Beard Woodcutter turned back, mustered his power, and knocked down three or four people with three punches and two kicks. The others also ran away. Beard Woodcutter then returned to the boat, hoisted the sails, and sailed downwind. By the time the second group of people arrived, the wind was strong and the water was swift, and Beard Woodcutter had already taken Zou girl to Chen Xueqi's house.

When Chen Xueqi and his wife met, there is no need to describe their joy and sorrow. They were so grateful to Beard Woodcutter that they were willing to risk their lives for him. After this incident, Beard Woodcutter's reputation for righteousness and helping those in need grew even greater.

A few years later, Li Zicheng broke through Beijing, and Emperor Chongzhen died on Meishan Mountain. People in the village were saying, "Li Zicheng has become the emperor!"

Beard Woodcutter initially didn't believe it, but after asking a few people, they all said the same thing. Beard Woodcutter was furious and jumped up and down, shouting, "I only know that the emperor's surname is Zhu. What is Li Zicheng that he should become the emperor? Where has my emperor gone? Aren't there any civil and military officials in the Qing Dynasty who can save the emperor? Are these people just going to eat and take money and then become subjects of the thief? Your Majesty, I am old and cannot kill the thieves, so I can only repay you with my death! Your Majesty, wait for me, I am coming!"

Beard Woodcutter ran to the edge of Taihu Lake in one breath. He looked at the vast water, then looked up and shouted "Heaven!" three times. With a "plop," he jumped into Taihu Lake, causing a burst of bubbles. Beard Woodcutter was finished. Beard Woodcutter was already in his sixties when he died.

George Stephenson (1781-1848) 175

— Li Jizhen

He went from being the lowest miner to an engineer, from being illiterate to a great scientist, with no other secret than:

Learn how to do it—only fearing you don't understand

Ask why—not fearing others' ridicule

George Stephenson was born on June 9, 1781, in a village near Newcastle, England. His father was a coal miner, and his income was not even enough to feed his family, so he certainly couldn't afford his children's education. At the age of nine, Stephenson was sent to be a shepherd to ease his father's burden. A few years later, his father took him to the mine to do odd jobs, and he was assigned to clean the steam engine. While cleaning the steam engine, he studied its structure and quickly became familiar with it. He made models of various machines out of clay, which were so lifelike and well-made that everyone who saw them praised his skill.

The foreman in the mine saw that he was meticulous and hardworking and liked him very much, so he promoted him to be in charge of the water pump. The most frightening thing in the mine was water. If the water was not pumped out and allowed to rise, it could immediately cause a disaster, drowning the miners, destroying the mineral deposits, and potentially ruining the entire project. Fortunately, James Watt had already invented the water pump at that time, which was inexpensive and highly efficient, and was the only effective tool for preventing flooding in the mine. Stephenson became a water pump worker. Seeing the automatic up-and-down movement of the water pump, he was very surprised and wondered all day long: "Why can the fire in the furnace turn the water in the pot into steam? Why can steam make the whole machine turn?" He pondered and worried but could not figure out the reason, so he had to ask other colleagues. Several people he asked did not understand the reason. One day, he asked an experienced worker. The old man glared at him and scolded him, "What nonsense are you talking about, kid! If you keep daydreaming like this instead of working honestly, who would want to hire you? Just wait and see, you'll starve to death before you reach my age." After a while, he proudly held up three fingers to Stephenson and said, "I've been a worker for thirty years and have never been unemployed for a single day, entirely because I'm content with my lot, mind my own business, don't try to climb high, and don't think of good things. Good boy, learn from me!"

Stephenson was very angry when he heard this and couldn't help but retort, "Learn from you! What future is there in learning from you? A person should always do something worthwhile in life. How can you be a slave to bread for the rest of your life?" The old worker did not expect this child to dare to argue with him and immediately became angry out of embarrassment. He grabbed Stephenson's hair and asked, "Worthwhile child, tell me! Tell me! What is a worthwhile thing?" Stephenson did not want to argue with him and quickly shook off his hand and ran away. Unexpectedly, he stumbled and, after running only a few dozen steps, bumped into an engineer. The engineer thought Stephenson was causing some trouble and did not accept his apology, but called him back. The old worker saw this from afar and was very happy. He thought this child's job was definitely broken this time. Who knew that after the engineer understood the whole story, he liked Stephenson's eagerness to learn and explained to him: "Water turns into steam when heated, and steam has power that can drive the machinery, making the whole machine turn. This simple principle of steam has already been explained by Watt, but unfortunately, you are illiterate, so you don't know. You should try to find some time to study. All the important principles in the world are in books. You won't be able to understand them if you don't study."

At this time, Stephenson was already nineteen years old and did not know a single character. He felt very uncomfortable after hearing the engineer's words and couldn't sleep all night thinking about it. He scolded himself: "We are all illiterate, all fools. One fool is no better than another. Why did I argue with that old man today? I want to do something worthwhile, but if I'm illiterate, I won't understand the principles. How can I do anything?" He hated himself for being illiterate and unable to do worthwhile things, pinching himself and hitting himself like a madman. Finally, he figured it out and jumped out of bed happily, saying, "What's the rush? I just need to study hard. Although I'm already nineteen years old now, if I can work twice as hard as others, won't I be able to catch up with the educated men of my age in ten years?" So he was determined to study hard, working in the mine during the day and attending night school in the evening. He started reading ABCs in the same class as six- or seven-year-old children. The children saw that he was so old and just starting to read and laughed at him, calling him "Big Fool." He started reading from ABCs and learning to count from one, two, three. He pronounced the sounds with his forehead straight, and when he read, it sounded like he was hawking goods, which made the teacher and classmates couldn't help but laugh. He wanted to use the ability to read to help him do worthwhile things, so he didn't care about anything, wasn't shy, wasn't afraid of difficulties, and only knew how to bow his head and work hard. Because he worked so hard, he naturally made extraordinary progress. In just a few years, he understood all the scientific principles. So he decided that scientific invention was the most worthwhile thing to do and began to study steam engines.

In the past, he was amazed by Watt's water pump. Now, after some research, he felt that it was too crude. One day, he said to the engineer who had previously advised him to study, "Sir, look, Watt's water pump can never pump the water completely dry. Do you know the reason?" The engineer thought Stephenson was asking a foolish question again because of his ignorance and laughed, "If I knew the reason, I would be an inventor too." Stephenson was embarrassed to say the reason when he heard the engineer say this. Finally, he couldn't help but break his silence and boldly led the engineer to the water pump, pointing out the shortcomings here and there and explaining how it could be improved. The engineer felt that what Stephenson said made some sense and agreed to give him a chance to experiment. After the engineer left, Stephenson's colleagues surrounded him and laughed, saying, "Friend, you are just a worker, not an engineer. Don't overestimate yourself and make a fool of yourself. Improve the machine? Many top-notch engineers have no way. Stop daydreaming!"

Stephenson knew that it was useless to argue with ignorant people. He just smiled and didn't say anything. After everyone went off work, he started his experiment. After a few days, the mine was dry, without any water accumulation, and all the workers were able to work conveniently because of this. They were surprised and happy and went around asking who had done this good deed. When they found out that Stephenson had improved the water pump, everyone was shocked. From then on, not only did no one (including the old worker who had offended Stephenson before) not respect Stephenson, but even the workers themselves knew how to respect themselves. The mine owner knew that Stephenson was a promising person and immediately promoted him to chief engineer.

There was another terrible disaster in the mine—floods. The mines used candles, and the flames were not shielded, so they often came into contact with violent or highly flammable gases, causing explosions or fires, which often killed countless people. In order to protect his colleagues and repay the mine owner's recognition, Stephenson invented a safety lamp to replace candles. But he believed that this was only the result of his preliminary research, and he refused to be complacent because of this. He wanted to do something great and be a great inventor. So he worked day and night to study steam engines. As a result, it took him fifteen years to invent the train and the railway, which facilitated transportation around the world and accelerated the progress of human civilization. His contribution is truly "immeasurable."

Publishing World

On the Problem of Textbooks 176

— Zhou Hanmei

The problem of textbooks in today's large, medium, and small schools has indeed reached a very serious point. Whether in the arts or sciences, when school authorities or instructors choose a textbook for a particular subject, they always find it extremely difficult and not easy to achieve satisfactory results. At the same time, even if they reluctantly choose a relatively suitable textbook, in fact, not only do the teachers still feel pain, but the students also feel all kinds of problems and have no interest in learning. Therefore, the impact on the level of students in general large, medium, and small schools is also conceivable.

Regarding textbooks for primary and secondary schools, although there are curriculum standards promulgated by the Ministry of Education to follow when compiling them, these curriculum standards only have general guidance. The right to choose and discard all materials still lies with the compilers themselves. At the same time, every textbook must be submitted to the Ministry of Education for review, but the main point of the review is to focus on the negative aspects, such as whether it violates the curriculum standards. Therefore, the key to the excellence of textbooks lies entirely with the compilers.

Now, let's take the Chinese textbooks for secondary schools as an example. The poverty and dryness of their content are really beyond expectations. As for the aspects of vernacular Chinese, then they are either works from the enlightenment era of one or two decades ago or awkward and tortuous translations. As for the aspects of classical Chinese, then articles from Guwen Guanzhi, Zhan Guo Ce, Li Sao, and Shi Ji are adopted in large quantities. As for the literature of the last ten years, it is simply rare. As a result, middle school students find writing very difficult. Junior high school students who read a lot of vernacular Chinese write articles that learn from those awkward and tortuous translations, describing moonlight that goes all the way from quicksilver to neon lights, and describing walking that goes all the way from the swaying of willow branches to incense-burning old women. High school students who read a lot of classical Chinese can't catch up with even one millionth of the literary spirit of the Eight Great Masters of the Tang and Song dynasties, let alone the writing style of Li Sao and Shi Ji. It's simply impossible to get even a smooth classical Chinese article for newspaper reporting. Speaking of this, the author must solemnly state that it is not to say that the articles in the current Chinese textbooks are all undesirable, but to say why not adopt more modern literature as articles for middle school students to recite? Why are middle school students made to study in detail articles that are at least twenty years old, and as many as thousands of years old, away from modern thought? At the same time, the compilation style is also extremely ridiculous. The teachers who compile the textbooks don't know whether they are for the convenience of the teachers or to please the students? They often annotate and explain the difficult words and sentences one by one. As a result, the teachers don't have to prepare, and the students can save on buying a dictionary. I don't know if this method is ultimately beneficial or harmful to middle school students? Taking middle school geography textbooks as an example, the part about products is always "coal and iron are very rich," "antimony, lead, and other minerals are very rich." The statistical figures are rare. Is it really impossible to find any statistical figures in China? Other examples include history textbooks, which do not focus on scientific explanations when describing ancient society, but still talk about the creation of heaven and earth; the changes of dynasties do not focus on the socio-economic system, but still record a running account of the imperial family. Such examples are too numerous to mention! How can such textbooks not be considered misleading children? This is from the content of middle school textbooks. If we take a closer look at the textbooks of universities and primary schools, there will certainly be many problems, which urgently need careful research and correction. As for the expensive pricing of textbooks, it is also worth our serious attention. Now, a textbook of about one hundred pages is priced at least fifty or sixty cents, and at most seventy or eighty cents. Two volumes often cost about one dollar and forty or fifty cents, which is a great difficulty for the children of the average middle-class family.

The reason why the textbooks of large, medium, and small schools are so bad, I think, is also due to certain reasons. In order to compete commercially or for economic considerations, publishing houses either produce them crudely and hastily due to time constraints or fail to hire people with rich knowledge and experience due to remuneration issues. This has led to today's phenomenon. Excellent teachers who teach in large, medium, and small schools often have no time for this due to the pressure of life. As a result, teachers cannot make significant contributions, and publishing houses cannot have satisfactory achievements.

Regarding the issue of textbooks, the author often has a dream, which I might as well write here for the reference of the educational administration authorities: I think that to hope that the textbooks of large, medium, and small schools are excellent, the highest educational administration agency should bear a kind of responsibility, that is, the work of compiling textbooks should be the responsibility of the government. Divide the country's provinces and cities into several educational districts (the division of districts is based on the differences in cultural level). Set up a national university, a national middle school, and a national primary school in each educational district. Raise the salaries of teachers as much as possible, reduce the teaching hours as much as possible, and give them job security. Give them the responsibility of compiling textbooks for large, medium, and small schools. After compiling the textbooks for large, medium, and small schools in one or two years, hand them over to major Chinese publishing houses for distribution on the one hand, and ask teachers from large, medium, and small schools across the country to strictly criticize them on the other hand. Of course, these sets of textbooks are not immutable, as the fixed editions of each educational district, but must be revised every year and supplemented every year. The author firmly believes that as long as the methods are careful and the selection of talents is strict, the serious problem of textbooks can be solved, and we can reach our ideal state.

"Wartime Economics" 177

— Duxiu

A.C. Pigou, original author, Xu Zongshi, translator, Commercial Press publication

——The crisis of the Second World War is obviously approaching. The efforts of various countries to expand their military preparations, the increasing prosperity of the military industry, and the active advancement of wartime preparations, all the disputes, all the contradictions, need a general solution and general liquidation through war. Although people all over the world, in view of the cruelty, sacrifice, and horror of the First World War, have a psychology of fearing war, whether the Second World War will break out does not depend on whether people in general fear war or not, but depends on the interests of the general financial groups and the intentions of ambitious people. At the same time, in the east and west of this earth, we have heard that a powder keg is about to explode, but the powder keg in the East is much more serious and critical than the one in the West. For the sake of the fate of the country and the survival of the nation, people across the country should begin preparations for a very special period. Then, wartime economics, which determines the victory or defeat of the overall war situation, must be deeply studied.

Xu Zongshi's translation of A.C. Pigou's "Wartime Economics," although the original author cannot escape the confines of liberal economics, and also emphasizes the situation in the UK during the European era, whether in time or place, there is a sense of being too far away, but this practical lesson is always a very valuable page. Moreover, it encompasses rich content, and the theory is well-organized, which is certainly not comparable to the general ordinary special books that record the economic and financial situation in Europe at that time. Therefore, the author believes that this book must be solemnly introduced to the general readers.

The contents of the book are divided into the following eighteen chapters: First, Introduction; Second, The Impact of War; Third, The Economic Causes of War; Fourth, The Resources of War; Fifth, The Real and Monetary Sacrifices and Expenses of War; Sixth, The Choice of Personal Austerity; Seventh, Government Requisition; Eighth, Taxation and Public Debt; Ninth, Methods of Raising Free Public Debt; Tenth, Methods of Manufacturing Bank Credit to Raise War Expenses; Eleventh, Price Control; Twelfth, Quantitative Allocation of Consumers; Thirteenth, Quantitative Allocation of Raw Materials Purchased with Priority and Factories; Fourteenth, Subsidies; Fifteenth, Rehabilitation of Currency and Exchange; Sixteenth, Management of Imported Goods and Foreign Investment; Seventeenth, Rehabilitation of Internal Debt; Eighteenth, Government Control Issues After the War. In these eighteen chapters, the author takes into account both theory and practice, and elaborates in detail. Although most of them focus on the situation in the UK, there are many things that can be used as a reference for our country. The book has two hundred and forty-two pages, more than one hundred thousand words, and is priced at one dollar and three cents, published by the Commercial Press.

Publication Award 178

— Zhang Tianyi

——A suggestion——

The desolation of the publishing industry is a fact. It is also a fact that there have been no great works in philosophy, science, literature, etc. in recent years. There are certainly many reasons for this, but the author believes that in addition to negative criticism and positive guidance, the government should have the necessity to set up "publication awards."

In any country, assuming that considerable attention is paid to cultural undertakings, then material rewards such as academic subsidies and subsidies must be spared no effort. However, in China, there is currently no such method, which we cannot but consider a great regret!

According to the author's view, the Chinese government should set up "publication awards," divided into departments such as philosophy, politics, economics, education, international relations, chemistry, physics, and literature. If there are books in the above-mentioned professional theories that are explained in a given year, and the content is very excellent and qualified by expert review, then in addition to the author receiving the bonus, the publishing agency should also be given material rewards.

Its benefits can make publishing houses more diligent in their own business, writers more diligent in their own research, and the academic atmosphere in the country can also be improved and cultivated.

Supplement to Shenbao Local Edition

Commentary

Rickshaw Pullers Welfare Association 179

— Jianping

Earlier this month, the rickshaw owners were dissatisfied with the authorities' firm implementation of rent reduction, and stopped parking their vehicles to strike in protest. The rickshaw puller turmoil lasted for three consecutive days, and order was restored only on the 4th when the rickshaw owners accepted the reduction method, but the losses on both sides had reached more than 100,000 yuan. The rickshaw owners are to blame, so there is no need to say more. As for the rickshaw pullers who eat what they earn every day, they suffered invisible unemployment due to the rickshaw owners stopping their vehicles, and this loss cannot be calculated. At that time, the commentators unanimously expressed dissatisfaction with both parties manipulating and using rickshaw pullers, and proposed reducing rents and abolishing the membership fees paid by rickshaw pullers to the mutual aid association. However, due to the rickshaw owners' surrender, the turmoil was temporarily ended, and only God knows the invisible losses suffered by the rickshaw pullers in the past three days.

The next problem that arose was the restriction on registration. Rickshaw pullers are really doomed to have many misfortunes. One wave has not subsided, and another wave has risen. On the 15th, the unemployed rickshaw pullers were registered. Due to vehicle restrictions, only 5,000 people could be supplemented to fill the vacancies, while the number of unemployed people reached 30,000 to 40,000. As a result, a big commotion occurred, resulting in the destruction of fifteen trams and cars, and many people were injured. The eleven arrested rickshaw pullers, including Mei Hongzhong, were sentenced on the 27th. They were convicted of "disturbing order" and sentenced to fifty days of detention. The cause of this dispute was the restriction on registration, and the reason why the unemployed rickshaw pullers rioted was nothing more than to make a living by any means. Therefore, the biggest reason is that the authorities have not paid attention to the suffering of the rickshaw pullers.

Now, the Rickshaw Pullers Association of the Special Zone is seeking to organize a rickshaw pullers welfare association from party and government agencies. Needless to say, we also know that this is an organization that handles rickshaw pullers' welfare affairs. And in the evening newspaper on the 27th, we have seen the preparatory meeting of the welfare association, and the following three items were resolved—1. The location of the association is decided to be in the Nanyang Bridge area. 2. The expenses shall be borne by the contractors in each district. 3. The association should handle the guarantee of rickshaw pullers' work based on factual needs. It was also decided to first launch two items: "Theft Car Guarantee" and "Vehicle Safety Insurance."

After reading their resolutions and the two welfare undertakings that were launched first, we believe that they have failed to fulfill the responsibility of this welfare association. We believe that all welfare undertakings should start from the most urgent aspects, and it is necessary to deeply understand the suffering of rickshaw pullers. Regarding the suffering of rickshaw pullers, in addition to the inability of unemployed rickshaw pullers to maintain their lives, such as the turmoil caused by the infighting between the Car Committee and the rickshaw owners, which caused great suffering, and the inhuman treatment they receive daily, as well as the collection of membership fees from the mutual aid association, etc., are all urgent issues that need to be resolved. As for all insurance undertakings, educational undertakings, entertainment undertakings, etc., they can only be discussed after relieving the current suffering. Otherwise, abandoning the relief of the current suffering and only seeking that empty and unrealistic welfare undertaking, what welfare can be said to the rickshaw pullers themselves?

Lane 180

— Zhuo Er

Low, cramped houses huddled together, forming this small alley, looking almost like a group of ragged, filthy, and hunchbacked old beggars. Matted, messy hair, revealing gaunt faces covered in wrinkles, bodies laden with filth, emitting a foul odor, and constantly waving arms covered in sores, as if begging someone for something... The alley crouches in the darkness like in a season without sunlight, flashing hateful eyes, chasing after a gray fate.

It's not strange that people live here, like in other places, but what sets it apart is that only women reside here. Men only come to satisfy certain desires. They have no husbands, no families, no hierarchical distinctions. They are a group determined by the conditions of life, engaging in the same means of survival. Their lives continue in segments, and within each "segment," they complete a unit of transaction. Yesterday it was like this, today it is like this, and tomorrow it will be like this, continuing on and on...

The low houses let in no sunlight at all (the sunlight is blocked by the high walls standing in front). So inside, everything is only vague, filled with a black mist. The walls are damp, and the base of the walls is covered with moss and fungi. The damp smell permeates the air, assaulting the nasal passages, making one feel suffocated and uncomfortable, or even want to vomit, but they are completely unfazed!

Morning here replaces night, but at night, this place becomes the most active. At this time, the pulse of their lives beats at a high speed.

"Let's go, let's go to the lane!"

Hardworking, single men, having finished their day's work, with tired hearts, seek comfort from them. In the hazy night, they search for suitable companions...

They stand under the dim streetlights in the alley, singing coarse and simple love songs, their voices so low and hoarse, with a broken tremor. They flaunt their charms to the single men, hoping to gain someone's favor. So they further adorn themselves, transforming themselves to be significantly different from others, so that they are easily noticed. They compete with each other, vying for beauty in the dark.

A'gen Sao, almost forty years old, is one of the oldest in the alley. She probably came here in her teens. She has spent decades of gray years here. She knows that this is a disreputable profession, but when she thinks that there is no other way to make a living, she feels at ease. Instead, she thinks engaging in this profession is right, sacred, and does not diminish her personality. So she cleverly shifts to another thought, lightly saying, "Fate..."

This fate plays with the women in the alley.

A'gen Sao, like her young and pretty companions, dresses herself a bit cleaner, applies powder and rouge to her face. She tries her best to appear young and pretty, to win the love of young men, swaying her fat body, chasing after every man.

"Sir, sir, come and have some fun! It's very pleasant..."

Her voice is as hoarse as a male duck, mixed with a plea in its softness. Like this, she surrounds every man, following closely. But, those young men disappoint her. They only glance up and down at her, then burst out laughing. They only tease her, saying, "Are you eighty years old?... You old grandma..." They abandon her, ignoring her, and leave with young women in their arms!

She numbly loses every hope. She quickly catches up to another man who comes to the alley: "Have pity on me! Kind sir: "Would you like to sit in my house for a while, sir...?" "...Very cheap, sir..."

How hard are their hearts! They quickly escape her entanglement. Her pitiful pleas only earn her many frivolous slanders! Those young companions who have obtained customers smile ingratiatingly at the customers, swaying their waists, making malicious faces at her as they pass by. She dares not look directly at their proud appearance. She turns her head aside. Her heart is filled with bursts of severe pain, as if someone is cutting it into pieces, slice by slice...

Everything before her eyes is blurred by tears.

--"I am not good anymore! I no longer have the ability to compete with my younger companions..." she thinks this. "...I, I was also so young before!... I was also welcomed by men, but now it is over, forgotten like the old women of the past..."

"The young women of today will also grow old one day..."

She feels indescribably sad in her heart, and at the same time, she sees the future fate of her young companions.

"If only this alley didn't exist one day!

Page 20

..." she mutters softly.

Looking up at the sky, it is pitch black with not a trace of light. The dilapidated and small houses are made to appear even shorter under the backdrop of the dark sky, as if about to collapse.

Vulgar words of flirtation, unrestrained, playful laughter crawl out from every room: and waves of shallow, lewd ditties rise and fall, disturbing the quiet of the alley. Few people walk in the alley. A'gen Sao knows that there is no hope again today. She wanders aimlessly.

"Let these houses all collapse together and crush these people to death!..." she says hatefully.

After Viewing "Thunderstorm" 181

— Li Yi

The China Traveling Theatre Troupe Performs at the Carlton

When "Thunderstorm" was performed by the Fudan Drama Society, I wrote some impressions. Due to the script's tight and vivid structure, the personality of each character was well grasped, coupled with a not bad performance, I was more moved than when I read the script. Now, four months later, I have the opportunity to see the performance of the professional "China Traveling Theatre Troupe," which moved me again.

Mr. Cao Yu, the author of "Thunderstorm," once said in an article about how he wrote "Thunderstorm" that he intended to have a "prologue" and an "epilogue" (although there are no these two scenes in the current performance, it is not difficult for us to get a glimpse of the author's creative attitude.) He said: "Simply put, it is to send the theatergoers home with a sorrowful mood, heads bowed, thinking deeply, thinking about these people who are tormented in passion, dreams, and calculations. What should be rippling in their hearts is a water-like sorrow, endless, rather than a feeling of confusion and terror, recalling Thunderstorm like a nightmare; death, pain like a pair of pliers clamping the heart, unable to catch a breath. In short, it is to "guide the audience's emotions into a wider sea of ​​contemplation."

Because of this, the author is like "old fathers whose faces are engraved with the wrinkles of experience, in the gloomy ancestral hall, vividly telling the story of the ghostly fire on the grave and the zombies in the wild temple," the listeners feel "fear creeping up their skin, and it seems that swaying ghost shadows flicker in the corners of the wall," but the story can be "vividly told," as if it is "a very distant place in time."

Therefore, although "Thunderstorm" exposes the sins of a large family, the author "did not consciously realize that I (the author, hereinafter the same) wanted to correct, satirize, or attack anything. Perhaps writing to the end vaguely felt a kind of majestic surge pushing me, I was venting suppressed anger, slandering Chinese families and society."

It is said that when the "China Traveling Theatre Troupe" rehearsed "Thunderstorm" in North China, the author personally participated and contributed his opinions. Therefore, if we say that it is faithful to the original work, then it can probably be said to be "faithful" (for example, the ending of the fourth act is the same as the original.) However, in my personal opinion, comparing it with the performance of Fudan, I feel that Fudan's revision is tighter, especially the end of the fourth act, and Lu Dahai's departure, are much more powerful than this version!

In terms of performance skills, the "China Traveling Theatre Troupe" is better than "Fudan." The reason it is better is because of their proficiency and their average. Lighting, sound effects, and stage design have generally reached the point where they are impeccable, and the acting skills of the actors are all above average, with nothing particularly unwatchable.

The best actors are Zhao Huishen, who plays Fanyi, and Jiang Ming, who plays Lu Gui. It is particularly commendable that Fanyi, such a difficult character to play, can be played to this extent. It is also very difficult to play Lu Gui so "just right." The actor who plays Sifeng, if he pays more attention to the lines, pays attention to the emotions of each sentence, and does not raise the last two words particularly high, will definitely have better achievements. The actor who plays Lu Dahai lacks a burly figure, his pronunciation lacks grandeur, and it is best not to comb his hair so shiny. The makeup of the actor who plays Lu's mother is a bit less elderly, and it is best to pay more attention to the movements and pronunciation. Zhou Ping is as difficult to play as Fanyi, and he has not grasped his entire personality here. He only performs according to the plot, and although he performs well in this section, he cannot connect with people in the overall impression. The actor who plays Zhou Chong not only has to make people feel that he is silly, but also has to make people feel his purity and innocence, and the beautiful ideals hidden in the depths of his soul. The gentleman now seems to lack some. The actor who plays Zhou Puyuan has enough action, but in terms of speaking, it is best not to drag out the sound of the words too long.

Apart from that, as I said above: lighting, sound effects, and devices have generally reached the point where they are impeccable. Especially in the third act, in the croaking of frogs, lightning, rain, and spring tunes, it makes people feel intimately like they are in a sultry summer night.

The "China Traveling Theatre Troupe," which has struggled for more than two years, has shown that they have not wasted their energy in this achievement. This is very gratifying. While we bless its growth, we hope that it, coming from the rapidly changing North China, can stand more firmly on the forefront of the drama movement, and face reality and the drama movement as a pioneer.

Frog 182

— Er He

"Ponds give birth to spring green, garden willows chirp with singing birds." The scenery of spring is indeed beautiful. During the day, there are many musicians and singers, playing or singing pleasant music, but at night they all stop playing and singing. Spring nights are lonely, quiet, except for the gentle spring breeze, the ripples of spring water, and the swaying of tree shadows, everything is peaceful and quiet. However, this is not absolute. That is the singing of frogs.

Frogs are lovable little creatures. They hide in a corner of the pond in their green clothes, making it difficult for people to see them. They have round, protruding eyes, like a poet wearing myopia glasses of five or six hundred degrees. Their strong legs are good at jumping. When they are resting in the grass, if you give them a slight shock, they will nimbly jump into the water with a "ge" sound, and then you can only see the splashing waves.

When I was young, I was very familiar with frogs. I used to imprison them with ropes and hurt them with guns, but after entering the city, I became estranged from them and didn't even have the heart to think about them. Last year, I returned to the countryside, listened to cicadas, listened to katydids, and now I hear the singing of frogs again. "Frogs are everywhere in the grassy pond," indeed, there are many, many frogs in spring. But most people hate them because they disturb people's sleep. Also, because their meat is delicious and edible, they often suffer the fate of being caught. I love frogs, but I have also eaten frog meat. That was six or seven years ago. I was in a school in the countryside. The scenery of the school was excellent. The school was surrounded by a large pond. There were especially many frogs in the pond. When we finished our night classes and went to the campus to play and sing, the frogs would respond to us, "Ge ge ge! Yue ge ge!" Rhythmically, they made us feel great pleasure. But when we went to sleep, everyone felt that the frogs were hateful. So one day, we hired five or six fishermen to catch them. In addition to giving them to the fishermen, we had a good dish that we had never had before. It was a large pot of frog meat, which was fresh and fragrant, and the taste was authentic. The students all hoped to eat this good dish again. But at night, when I heard the sparse sound of frogs, I felt sad and repented. Since then, in the countryside and in the city, I have had opportunities to eat frogs, but I have never eaten them, although I know that the taste of frogs is authentic.

Now I hear the sound of frogs again. This wave of repentance is still attacking me. I love frogs. Frogs are optimistic poets. Autumn is the season with the most poets, but it is too sad after all. Mr. Zheng Zhenduo said in "Cicadas and Katydids": "They sing the song of autumn, the song of old age, and the song of farewell. Their songs are like the autumn wind sweeping away fallen leaves, the mournful women playing the pipa, lonely and strange, clear and lingering, low and full of sorrow." These are excellent words to describe the poets of autumn. As for the spring poet, the frog, that is not the case. Their voices are spacious and bright. They don't complain about heaven or blame others. They raise their heads and sing, passionately and generously. When they sing alone, they are like a disheveled poet standing in the wilderness, singing his open-minded poems. When a few of them sing together, sparsely, they are like large raindrops falling on umbrella-like lotus leaves. When they sing in groups, it is even better, like the evening tide on the Qiantang River, rolling in. But whether they sing alone, in groups, or in crowds, their hearts are always broad, and they have no sad and declining sounds.

"Ducks are the first to know when the spring river warms up." In fact, the frog's sensitivity is no less than that of a duck. When they immerse their whole bodies in the water, they have long known that the water is warm. All the insects have not yet sung, but the frogs have already sung. Frogs are the praisers and pioneers of spring.

In the evening, when you are leisurely sitting on a chair smoking, when you are lying lonely on the bed thinking, or when you want to write a poem, or when you are tired of talking to your lover, or when you can't bear the sorrow, then, my friend; I advise you to close your eyes, suppress the beating of your heart, and listen to the frogs singing...

Drama 183

Insect Sound Society

Cast

A Wasp

Listen... you... I tell you this is really an interesting thing!

Mrs. Ji, who specially rushed from the south to Peiping to see her son, Mr. Ji, who is sick, is now sending her son to write a letter to her family, telling them the date of her return to the South.

Besides wanting to see her son's illness, she originally wanted to fulfill two wishes, which was to find a wife for her son... However, this disappointed her. Her son did not like to marry...

Guess what!

Mr. Ji does not like too old women, nor does he like too new ladies. This is difficult!

During this period, when Mr. Ji recovered from his illness in the hospital, the old lady became sick in the same hospital.

She also became acquainted with Miss Yu, the nurse in the hospital. Because she was sick for a week, her nephew came to see her several times. Did her nephew fall in love with Miss Yu? Therefore, before she returned to the South, she was determined to have this old lady act as a matchmaker.

She really felt strange. Her son, Mr. Ji, was so indifferent to marriage? And her nephew was so anxious, on the contrary.

Beep! Miss Yu is here. What is Miss Yu like! Miss Yu half agreed.

Hey! I won't say: guess what!

Her nephew is so anxious because he is in love with Miss Yu, however, her son, Mr. Ji, is also indifferent because he is in love with Miss Yu.

Mr. Ji has been sick for an extra week because of this.

While the old lady went upstairs to change her clothes. The two of them are...

Hard to say. —Listen!

A wasp bit Miss Yu, causing her to scream!

Don't you think this is too much?...

Film

British Historical Epic "The Iron Duke" 187

Shanghai Grand Theater Premieres Tonight at 9:15 PM

The famous British historical event "The Iron Duke" has now been made into a mega-film by the British film giant Gaumont Film Company at a cost of tens of thousands of dollars. The film stars George Arliss, a veteran of the British film industry, playing the leading role in a domestic film for the first time. Due to certain reasons, the film was banned from being screened by the concession authorities. Now, the Shanghai Grand Theater on North Sichuan Road will premiere it on Thursday, April 30, at 9:15 PM as the only theater in this city to show it. The plot of the film is very grand, depicting the historical events of the British general "Wellington" in the "Waterloo" war. It is a rare production in Wusong in recent years, and it is also a special film that only Fangyuan can show publicly. Seating has already begun. It is expected that the traffic on Qiujiang Road and North Sichuan Road will be heavy, and it will definitely cause a sensation.

"Waves Washing Sand" Miscellaneous Writings 188

Seashore, a deserted island, with surging waves washing the sand. After the sea water washes away, two skeletons are imprinted in the sand.

These two skeletons are victims of a conflict of interest. The theme of "Waves Washing Sand" begins with these two skeletons.

"Waves Washing Sand" not only has an extremely tense drama, but also writes about a great tragedy of mankind.

This tragedy will always exist among mankind and will not disappear. People have temporarily joined hands and made peace for their mutual interests, but when it comes to their respective interests, they will immediately turn against each other.

"Waves Washing Sand" is not only exceptionally meaningful in its theme, but also has special success in its portrayal, especially in its psychological depiction, which can be said to be meticulous.

It is also worth mentioning that this is the first sound film of Lianhua, and this sound film can be said to be a real attempt to exert the function of sound film.

Wu Yonggang only established his position in the art world with "The Goddess" and "Little Angel". The emergence of "Waves Washing Sand" is the stage where he achieves his greatest success.

Silver Screen Miscellany 189

Last year, the Yueming Company seemed to have hopes for great ambitions. It published special issues, raised funds, and made a lot of noise. When "Confusion" was released, it expanded its publicity. At the same time, the scenery films taken from Tibet were also prepared to be compiled into a script called "Panorama of Tibet." However, after not much time, it gradually faded. Finally, the company stopped operating invisibly, and the salaries of the employees were owed for several months, and it has been delayed until now. It seems that it is probably impossible to revive it like the Diantong Company. Moreover, news from reliable sources is that Xia Tianwu, Ren Pengnian's personal secretary, has entrusted lawyer Zhang Yifan to recover his arrears in salary, and other employees will also take similar actions. The outcome is temporarily unknown.

Zhaohua Film Company, which produced a film called "Tears of Remorse," once organized a song and dance troupe to run the docks, but the box office was a disastrous failure. The "Tears of Remorse" was involved in a lawsuit over the issue of transfer. Now, that publicity worker, Shi Tian, ​​using the name Hu Ang, is scheduled to open a cartoon exhibition on May 1st at Room 303, 3rd Floor, Continental Shopping Mall. However, his cartoons are different from others. They are drawn with ink brushes in the style of woodcuts. According to him, it is a new art form. These days, Mr. Shi Tian Hu Yiang has been very busy running around with his proud works.

Readers, if you have time, you can go to the Continental Shopping Mall tomorrow to broaden your horizons.
